leaderOpt.get(), currentTimeMs);\\n530:         return Optional.of(node);\\n531:     }\\n532: \\n533:     /**\\n534:      * Returns the set of IDs for {@link Node}s to which fetch requests should <em>not</em> be sent.\\n535:      *\\n536:      * <p>\\n537:      * When a partition has buffered data in {@link FetchBuffer}, that means that at some point in the <em>past</em>,\\n538:      * the following steps occurred:\\n539:      *\\n540:      * <ol>\\n541:      *     <li>The client submitted a fetch request to the partition's leader</li>\\n542:      *     <li>The leader responded with data</li>\\n543:      *     <li>The client received a response from the leader and stored that data in memory</li>\\n544:      * </ol>\\n545:      *\\n546:      * But it's possible that at the <em>current</em> point in time, that same partition might not be in a fetchable\\n547:      * state. For example:\\n548:      *\\n549:      * <ul>\\n550:      *     <li>\\n551:      *         The partition is no longer assigned to the client. This also includes when the partition assignment\\n552:      *         is either {@link SubscriptionState#markPendingRevocation(Set) pending revocation} or\\n553:      *         {@link SubscriptionState#markPendingOnAssignedCallback(Collection, boolean) pending assignment}.\\n554:      *     </li>\\n555:      *     <li>\\n556:      *         The client {@link Consumer#pause(Collection) paused} the partition. A paused partition remains in\\n557:      *         the fetch buffer, because {@link FetchCollector#collectFetch(FetchBuffer)} explicitly skips over\\n558:      *         paused partitions and does not return them to the user.\\n559:      *     </li>\\n560:      *     <li>\\n561:      *         The partition does not have a valid position on the client. This could be due to the partition\\n562:      *         awaiting validation or awaiting reset.\\n563:      *     </li>\\n564:      * </ul>\\n565:      *\\n566:      * For those reasons, a partition that was <em>previously</em> in a fetchable state might not <em>currently</em>\\n567:      * be in a fetchable state.\\n568:      * </p>\\n569:      *\\n570:      * <p>\\n571:      * Here's why this Request Building Stage:**\\nWhen a consumer calls poll(), it invokes Fetcher.sendFetches() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java:105). This method calls AbstractFetch.prepareFetchRequests() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AbstractFetch.java:412) to determine which partitions need to be fetched and construct FetchRequest.PartitionData for each partition, including topic IDs, fetch offsets, fetch sizes, and leader epochs. The requests are grouped by target broker node.\\n\\n**2. Fetch Request Builder Stage:**\\nFor each node with partitions to fetch, AbstractFetch.createFetchRequest() (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AbstractFetch.java:301) creates a FetchRequest.Builder.
